    舌门

    　　　　证治准绳 【明　王肯堂】

    　　　　　舌部所属

    　　属手少阴心经。
    　　 【注　《素问》曰：心在窍为舌，畏寒。《内经》曰：心气通于舌，心和则舌能知五味矣。病则舌卷短，颧赤，其脉搏坚而长。乔岳曰：心绝则舌不能收，及不能语。】　　又属足太阴脾经。[27p]

    Thirty-Fourth Tongue
    Referring to the illustration
    If the tongue appears gray-black with black stripes, and the pulse is strong, urgently use Da Chengqi Decoction to purge. If the pulse is floating and there is a thirst for water, use Liangge Powder to resolve it. Of ten cases, two or three can be saved.

    Thirty-Fifth Tongue
    Referring to the illustration
    If the root of the tongue is slightly black and the tip is yellow, and the pulse is slippery, it can be purged. If the pulse is floating, nurturing yin and expelling yang is necessary. If there is aversion to wind and cold, induce slight sweating using Shuangjie Powder. If there is diarrhea, use Detoxifying Decoction; eight to nine out of ten can be saved.

    Thirty-Sixth Tongue
    Referring to the illustration
    If the root of the tongue is slightly black, the tip is yellow with visible or faint stripes, and the pulse is strong, urgently use Da Chengqi Decoction to purge. If the pulse is floating and there is thirst for water, use Liangge Powder to resolve it; two or three out of ten can be saved.
    The above thirty-six tongues are quick methods for diagnosing cold damage. When encountering cases, apply with care, and there will be no mistakes.

    Tongue Classification

    Standard for Diagnosis and Treatment
    (Ming Dynasty, Wang Kengtang)

    Belonging to the Tongue
    It is related to the Hand Shaoyin Heart Meridian.
    [Note: The Suwen states: The heart connects to the tongue; it fears cold. The Nei Jing states: The heart qi communicates with the tongue; when the heart is harmonious, the tongue can recognize the five flavors. In illness, the tongue may retract and shorten, with redness in the cheeks, its pulse strong and long. Qiao Yue states: When the heart fails, the tongue cannot retract and cannot speak.]
    It also pertains to the Foot Taiyin Spleen Meridian.[27p]

    　　 【注　李东垣曰：舌者，心也，复能知味，是舌中有脾也。《灵枢》曰：足太阴之正，贯舌中。《素问》曰：中央黄色，入通于脾，故病在舌本。《灵枢》又曰：足太阴是动则病舌本强，所生病者舌本痛。又曰：刺舌下中脉太过，血出不止为喑。注舌下脉，脾脉也；瘖，不能言也。又孙景思曰：舌者，心气之所主，脾脉之所通，二脏不和，风邪中之则舌强不能言，壅热攻之则舌肿不能转。更有重舌、木舌、舌肿、出血等证，皆由心脾二经风热所乘而然也。】　　又兼属足阳明胃经。
    　　 【注　张鸡峰曰：脾胃主四肢，其脉连舌本而络于唇口。胃为水谷之海，脾气磨而消之，由是水谷之精化为营卫以养四肢。　若起居失节，饮食不时，则致脾胃之气不足，而营卫之养不周，风邪乘虚而干之，则四肢与唇口俱痹，语言蹇濇，久久不治，变为痿疾。经云：治痿独取阳明，谓足阳明也，治法宜多用脾胃药，少服去风药，则可安矣。】　　又属足少阴肾经。[28p]

    Note: Li Dongyuan said: The tongue is associated with the heart; it also knows taste, which indicates that the tongue contains elements of the spleen. In the "Ling Shu," it is said that the foot Taiyin connects to the middle of the tongue. The "Su Wen" states: The center is yellow, which corresponds to the spleen, hence ailments at the root of the tongue. The "Ling Shu" also mentions that the foot Taiyin, when active, causes tongue root stiffness, and illnesses arising will result in pain at the tongue root. Additionally, if the sublingual pulse is excessively needled, bleeding may occur, leading to muteness. The sublingual pulse is the spleen pulse; muteness refers to the inability to speak. Furthermore, Sun Jingsi stated: The tongue is governed by the heart’s qi and is connected to the spleen pulse. If the two organs are imbalanced, wind pathogens can invade, causing the tongue to stiffen and hinder speech, while phlegm heat attacks, leading to swelling and the inability to articulate. There are also symptoms such as heavy tongue, stiff tongue, tongue swelling, and bleeding, all resulting from the invasion of wind and heat on the heart and spleen channels.

    Additionally, it is also associated with the foot Yangming stomach meridian.

    Note: Zhang Jifeng stated: The spleen and stomach govern the four limbs, their pulses connecting to the root of the tongue and linking to the lips and mouth. The stomach is the sea of fluids, the spleen processes and digests them, whereby the essence of these fluids transforms into nutrient defenses to nourish the four limbs. If one fails to maintain proper living habits or eats at irregular times, it leads to insufficient spleen and stomach qi, resulting in poor nourishment for defense, allowing wind pathogens to invade, causing paralysis of both the limbs and the lips, resulting in slurred speech. If untreated for a long time, it could develop into atrophy. The classics state that treating atrophy should focus on the Yangming system, namely the foot Yangming, and the treatment should emphasize the use of spleen and stomach remedies while minimizing medications to dispel wind for stability.

    Additionally, it also belongs to the foot Shaoyin kidney meridian.[28p]

    　　 【注　《灵枢》曰：足少阴之正，直者系舌本。舌纵涎下烦悗，取足少阴。《元珠》曰：舌之下窍，肾之津液所朝也。注：下窍，廉泉穴也，一名舌本，在颔下结喉上　《素问》曰：刺足少阴脉重虚出血，为舌难以言。】　　又属足厥阴肝经。
    　　 【注　《灵枢》曰：肝者筋之合也，筋者聚于阴器，而脉络于舌本。】
    　　　　外科正宗 【明　陈实功】

    　　　　　痰包

    　　痰包乃痰饮乘火流行，凝注舌下，结如匏肿，绵软不硬，有妨言语，作痛不安，用利剪刀当包剪破，流出黄痰，若鸡子清稠粘难断，捺尽，以冰硼散搽之，内服二陈汤加黄芩、黄连、薄荷数服，忌煎炒火酒等件。
    　　　　　重舌

    　　大人小儿重舌，乃心火妄动发之，当以线针点刺患上，令出恶血，内服解毒泻心汤，外以冰硼散搽之。[29p]

    Phlegm Bag

    The phlegm bag is caused by phlegm and fluid rising with heat, condensing under the tongue, forming a soft, swollen mass similar to a gourd, which affects speech and causes pain and discomfort. It should be cut open with sharp scissors, allowing the yellow phlegm to flow out, which resembles thick, sticky egg white that is hard to break. After draining, apply ice-boron powder externally and internally take Erchen Decoction with added Huangqin, Huanglian, and Bohe over several doses while avoiding fried foods, strong alcohol, and similar items.

    Heavy Tongue

    In both adults and children, a heavy tongue is caused by the chaotic action of heart fire. One should prick the affected area with a needle to let out toxic blood and take a detoxifying decoction to clear the heart internally. Externally, apply ice-boron powder.[29p]

    　　　　　木舌

    　　紫舌、木舌，亦由心火而发，用飞盐加冰片少许，勤搽，出涎自愈。又有痰气结于舌上，成核作痛，硬强者，用线针点破出血，用冰硼散搽之。
    　　　　医方考 【明　吴昆】

    　　　　　舌病方论

    　　《本事方》云：　一士人夜归，其妻熟寝，士人撼之。妻问何事？不答。又撼之，其妻惊视之，舌肿已满口，不能出声。急访医，得一叟负囊而至，用药掺之，比晓复旧。问之，乃蒲黄一物。昆按《内经》曰：热胜则肿。此证必心脾之火并于舌，故令肿而满口。蒲黄性寒，能清气凉血，故愈。　　热证多舌出。有病愈而舌不能入者，以冰片分许，研末，掺其舌上，则入。所以舌出者，热实于内，而欲吐舌泄气也；所以不能入者，邪气久居，舌强而不柔和也。冰片味辛热而气清香，可以利窍，可以柔筋，可以泄气，故得之而舌入矣。　　有人舌肿，舒出口外，无敢医者。[30p]

    Wood Tongue

    Purple tongue, wood tongue, also arise from heart fire. Use a little flying salt and borneol, apply diligently, and saliva will flow, leading to healing. If phlegm accumulates on the tongue, causing a painful lump, and it is hard and stiff, use a thread needle to prick and draw blood, then apply ice borax powder.

    Discussion on Tongue Diseases

    According to the "Ben Shi Fang": A scholar returned home at night while his wife was asleep. He shook her, and when she asked what was the matter, he did not respond. He shook her again, and she looked at him in surprise, only to find her tongue swollen and filling her mouth, unable to speak. They urgently sought a doctor, who arrived carrying a pouch of medicine and mixed it for her, and by morning she had returned to her original condition. When asked, he revealed it was cattail pollen. Kun comments that "The inner canon" states: Excess heat causes swelling. This condition must arise from the combined fire of the heart and spleen affecting the tongue, causing swelling and filling the mouth. Cattail pollen is cold in nature and can clear qi and cool the blood, hence it cured her.

    In cases of heat syndrome, there is often protrusion of the tongue. When one recovers yet the tongue cannot retract, use a bit of borneol, grind it into powder, and apply it to the tongue, and then it can retract. The reason for the tongue's protrusion is that heat is truly present inside, and it seeks to expel the tongue to release qi; the reason it cannot retract is that the pathogenic qi has long been lodged, making the tongue stiff and not pliable. Borneol is spicy and warming but has a clear fragrance, which can open the orifices, soften the tendons, and release qi. Thus, with its application, the tongue retracts. There are instances of swollen tongues that extend outward where no one dares to treat them.[30p]

    一村人云：偶有此药，归而取至，乃二纸捻，以灯烧之，取烟熏舌，随即消缩。众问其方，村人曰：吾家旧有一牛，亦舌肿胀出口，人教以蓖麻油蘸纸作捻，烧烟熏之而愈，因以治人亦验。昆谓：舌肿舒出口外，经所谓热胜则肿也。然舌者心之苗，又脾之经络连舌本，散舌下，其热当责于心脾二经。《本草》云：蓖麻主浮肿恶气，取油涂之，叶主风肿不仁，捣蒸敷之，则其能解风肿内热也可知矣。然用其烟犹有妙义，烟乃轻清之物，一入于口，呼吸传变，可使径达心脾，匪惟治标，亦可疗本。村人用之而不达其理，斯其所以为村人。医者闻之而不察其理，则亦村人而已矣！[31p]

    A villager said: Occasionally there is this medicine; I returned home to fetch it, and found it to be two pieces of paper twisted into wicks. I burned them with a lamp to let the smoke waft over my tongue, and it immediately reduced the swelling. When others inquired about the method, the villager replied: In my family, there was an old cow whose tongue also became swollen and protruded. People taught to use castor oil to soak the paper wicks, burn them, and let the smoke treat it, which proved effective.

    Kun remarked: When the tongue is swollen and protruding, it is said that heat overwhelms and causes the swelling. The tongue is the seed of the heart, and the spleen's meridians are connected to the root of the tongue. Thus, the heat should be attributed to the heart and spleen meridians. The "Compendium of Materia Medica" states: Castor oil is effective for edema and eliminating foul gas; applying oil based on the leaves can alleviate wind swelling and numbness when pounded and steamed for application, which shows it can relieve internal heat from wind swelling.

    However, the use of its smoke has a subtle meaning: smoke is a light and clear substance; once it enters the mouth, it can be transmitted and transformed through breathing, allowing it to reach directly to the heart and spleen. It not only addresses the symptoms but can also treat the root cause. The villager used it without understanding the principle; that is why he remains a villager. If a physician hears of it and fails to discern its reasoning, he is also merely a villager![31p]

    　　　　景岳全书 【明　张介宾】

    　　　　　论胎色

    　　舌胎舌黑，虽云火证，然实火虚火俱能为之。凡治此者，但当察脉证，以虚实为主，而再以辨色之法参之，庶可无误。盖实热之黑，必兼红紫干渴，或多芒刺；若沉黑少红而带润滑者，本非实热证也。若其六脉细弱，而形困气倦，则又最为虚候，是必寒水乘心火不归原之病，此不救本而但知治标，则万无一生矣。此之治法：凡里热未甚而表散有未解者，宜柴胡诸饮之类，以解其表；里邪热甚者，宜凉膈散、犀角地黄汤之类以清其内，此治实热之法也。[32p]

    On Fetal Color

    A black tongue in a fetus, although said to indicate fiery symptoms, can actually result from both true and false heat. When addressing this condition, one should primarily observe the pulse to distinguish between true and false, and then use color differentiation as a secondary tool to avoid mistakes. Generally, true heat causing blackness will also show signs of red, purple, dry mouth, or several prickling sensations; if the black is deep with little red and is smooth, it does not indicate true heat. Conversely, if the six pulses are thin and weak, accompanied by a feeling of fatigue and depletion, this indicates a state of deficiency, suggesting that cold water is obstructing the heart's fire and not returning to its original state. Merely treating the symptoms without addressing the root cause guarantees an unsuccessful treatment.

    The treatment method: If the heat within is not severe and there’s still some unresolved exterior issue, one should use drinks like Chai Hu decoctions to resolve the exterior; if the internal heat is quite severe, use remedies like Liang Ge San or Xijiao Dihuang Tang to clear the interior. This is the method for treating true heat.[32p]

    若阴虚火盛，而兼有表邪未解者，宜补阴益气煎之类兼表里而治之；若形气病气俱不足，寒水乘心而虚阳不敛者，必用理阴煎、理中汤或大补元煎之类，以单救其里，自可保其无虞，此治虚火之法也。若舌有白胎，语言蹇濇者，以薄荷、白蜜同姜片，蘸而揩擦之。　　舌为心之官，本红而泽。凡伤寒三四日已后，舌上有胎必自润而燥，自滑而濇，由白而黄，由黄而黑，甚至焦干，或生芒刺，是皆邪热内传由浅入深之证也。故凡邪气在表，舌则无胎，及其传里，则津液干燥而舌胎生矣。若邪犹未深，其在半表半里之间，或邪气客于胸中者，其胎不黑不濇，止宜小柴胡之属以和之。若阳邪传里，胃中有热，则舌胎不滑而濇，宜栀子豉汤之属以清之。若烦躁欲饮水数升者，白虎加人参汤之类主之。[33p]

    If there is yin deficiency and excessive fire, accompanied by unresolved exterior pathogens, it is appropriate to use yin tonics and qi-boosting decoctions that address both exterior and interior. If both the form and qi are deficient, with cold water invading the heart and the empty yang not consolidating, one must use formulas like Li Yin Decoction, Li Zhong Decoction, or Great Nourishing Yuan Decoction to single-mindedly support the interior, which can safeguard against danger; this is the method to treat empty fire.

    If the tongue has a white coating and speech is slurred, one should use mint and white honey combined with ginger slices to apply and rub onto it. The tongue is the organ of the heart, normally red and moist. After three or four days of cold damage, if the tongue has a coating, it will inevitably turn from moist to dry, from slippery to rough, from white to yellow, from yellow to black, and even scorched dry, or develop pricking sensations; all these are signs of evil heat transmitting from the superficial to the deeper layers. Therefore, when the pathogenic qi is in the exterior, the tongue will not have a coating; when it transmits to the interior, the fluids become dry, leading to tongue coating formation.

    If the pathogenic influence is still not deep, existing between the exterior and interior, or if the pathogenic qi is lodged in the chest, the coating will not be black or rough, and one should only use formulas like Xiao Chai Hu Decoction to harmonize it. If the yang pathogens penetrate the interior, causing heat in the stomach, the tongue coating will be rough rather than slippery, necessitating formulas such as Zhi Zi Chi Decoction to clear it. If there is restlessness and a desire to drink large amounts of water, one should use White Tiger Decoction with Ginseng and similar formulas to address it.[33p]

    大都舌上黄胎而焦濇者，胃腑有邪热也，或清之或微下之。《金匮要略》曰：舌黄未下者，下之黄自去。然必大便燥实，脉沉有力而大渴者，方可下之。若微渴而脉不实，便不坚，胎不干燥芒刺者，不可下也。其有舌上黑胎而生芒刺者，则热更甚矣，宜凉膈散、承气汤、大柴胡之属酌宜下之。若胎色虽黑滑而不濇者，便非实邪，亦非火证，非惟不可下，且不可清也。此辨舌之概，虽云若此，然犹有不可概论者，仍宜详察如左。　　按伤寒诸书皆云：心为君主之官，开窍于舌。心主火，肾主水，黑为水色而见于心部，是为鬼贼相刑，故知必死。此虽据理之谈，然实有未必然者。[34p]

    Generally, a yellow coating on the tongue that is scorched indicates the presence of pathogenic heat in the stomach and intestines. It may be treated either by clearing it or by mildly purging. The "Essentials from the Golden Coffer" states: if the tongue is yellow but not purged, then purging will cause the yellow to disappear on its own. However, one must ensure that the stool is dry and firm, the pulse is deep, strong, and there is great thirst to consider purging. If there is only slight thirst, the pulse is weak, the stool is not hard, and the coating is not dry and prickly, purging is not appropriate.

    If the tongue has a black coating with prickles, the heat is even more intense, and it is advisable to use cooling medicines such as Liangge Powder, Chengqi Decoction, or Da-Chaihu Decoction accordingly. If the coating is black and slippery but not scorched, it indicates an absence of real pathogenic factors and is not a sign of fire; in this case, purging or attempting to clear it would not only be inappropriate but also harmful.

    This is a general differentiation based on the tongue, and while it is stated this way, there are still cases that do not fit neatly into these categories; therefore, careful examination is recommended as discussed below.

    It is noted in various treatises on febrile diseases that the heart is the sovereign organ, opening to the tongue. The heart governs fire, and the kidney governs water; black, being the color of water, appearing in the heart region indicates a conflict leading to death. Although this is a logical assertion, there are exceptions to it.[34p]

    夫五行相制，难免无克，此其所以为病，岂因克为病，便为必死？但当察其根本何如也。如黑色连地而灰黯无神，此其本源已败，死无疑矣。若舌心焦黑而质地红活，未必皆死证。阳实者清其胃火，火退自愈，何虑之有！其有元气大损而阴邪独见者，其色亦黄黑；真水涸竭者，其舌亦干焦。肾中水火俱亏，原非实热之证，欲辨此者，但察其形气脉色，自有虚实可辨，而从补从清，反如冰炭矣。故凡以焦枯干濇者，尚有非实非火之证。再若青黑少神而润滑不燥者，则无非水乘火位，虚寒证也。若认此为火，而苦寒一投，则余烬随灭矣。故凡见此者，但当详求脉证，以虚实为主，不可因其焦黑而执言清火也！伤寒固尔，诸证亦然。[35p]

    The Five Elements interact and restrain each other; it is inevitable that there will be overcoming, and this is why sickness arises. Is it because of overcoming that one must die? We must examine the root of the condition carefully. If there is black color touching the ground and looking gray and dull, its source is already ruined, and death is certain. However, if the tongue appears scorched and black but the texture is red and lively, it is not necessarily a sign of death. When yang energy is strong, it clears the stomach fire; if the fire recedes, healing will occur, so there is no need for concern! If there is great loss of vital energy and only yin pathogens are present, the color will also be yellow-black. If true water has dried up, the tongue will be dry and scorched as well. When both water and fire in the kidneys are deficient, it is not a sign of real heat. To discern this, one must observe the shape, energy, pulse, and color; the distinctions between deficiency and excess will become apparent, guiding one to tonify or clear accordingly, much like the difference between ice and fire. Therefore, anything that is scorched, dry, and withered may not indicate real heat or fire. Furthermore, if someone appears dark and lacking vitality but moist and not dry, it indicates that water is overcoming fire, which is a sign of deficiency-cold. Mistaking this for fire and administering bitter cold remedies would extinguish what little remains. Thus, for all such conditions, one must thoroughly investigate the pulse and symptoms, prioritizing deficiency and excess, rather than hastily concluding that the blackened appearance solely signifies clearing out heat! This applies to typhoid fever, and all other conditions similarly.[35p]

    　　　　　重舌木舌

    　　重舌木舌：以舌下肿出如舌，故曰重舌，又谓之子舌；忽肿木而硬者，谓之木舌，皆上焦热壅故也。惟宜砭针刺去其血为上策，及内服清胃降火之剂自愈。若舌忽肿起如猪胞，或硬如木石，不能出声，胀满塞口则闭闷杀人，但看舌下有如蝼蛄，或如卧蚕者，急于肿突处砭去其血，仍用釜底煤不拘多少，以盐酢调厚敷之，或用井华水调敷亦可。脱去更敷。如不甚者，单以此敷之亦愈。[36p]

    Swollen and Wooden Tongue

    Swollen and wooden tongue: It swells beneath the tongue and resembles the tongue itself, hence called swollen tongue, also referred to as "child's tongue." When it suddenly swells and becomes hard like wood, it is called wooden tongue; both conditions arise from heat and obstruction in the upper burner. The best method is to use a needle to prick and remove the blood, along with taking internal remedies to clear the stomach and reduce fire for recovery. If the tongue suddenly swells like a pig's bladder or becomes as hard as wood or stone, rendering speech impossible and causing fullness that blocks the mouth, it can be life-threatening. One should check beneath the tongue for signs resembling a mole cricket or a silkworm. In such urgent cases, blood should be pricked from the swollen area, and then a mixture of coal from the bottom of a pot with salt and vinegar should be thickly applied, or well water can be used to prepare a paste for application as well. After removal, reapply. If the condition is not severe, just using this application can lead to recovery.[36p]

    　　　　石室秘箓 【清　陈土铎】

    　　　　　生疮

    　　人口中忽生疮于舌上，吐出在外寸余，上结成黄靥，难以食物，人以为病在心也，心热故生此疮，此亦近理之谈而不知非也。亦有祟以凭之也。方用冰片一分入在蚌口内，立化为水，乃以鹅翎敷扫其上，立刻收入其舌，便可饮食矣。蚌乃至阴之物，攻至阴之邪，则邪自退走；况又加以冰片之辛温，逐邪不遗余力，自然手到功成也。　　口舌生疮，乃心火郁热，而舌乃心苗，故先见比证。法用黄连三钱，菖蒲一钱，水煎服一剂而愈，神方也。[37p]

    Stone Chamber Secret Manuscript
    [Qing Dynasty - Chen Tuduo]

    Sore in the Mouth

    A sore unexpectedly appears on the tongue inside the mouth, extending outward by an inch, forming a yellow scab on the surface. It makes eating difficult, and people believe the illness is in the heart, attributing it to internal heat causing this sore. This is indeed a common understanding, but it is not entirely accurate. There are also malevolent forces that may be involved.

    A proper method is to take a small amount of borneol, place it inside a clam shell, and it will immediately dissolve into water. Then, a goose feather should be used to apply it on the sore; it can quickly be absorbed into the tongue, enabling eating and drinking again. The clam is an extremely Yin substance, so it attacks Yin-related evils, causing them to retreat. Furthermore, the pungent warmth of borneol helps drive out evils vigorously, ensuring success with little effort.

    Sores on the tongue signify the presence of heat from the heart, and since the tongue is associated with the heart, it’s first seen as a connection. The method involves using three grams of Scutellaria (huanglian) and one gram of Acorus (changpu), boiled in water and taken as a single dose for recovery; this is a divine formula.[37p]

    此方不奇在黄连，而奇在菖蒲。菖蒲引心经之药，黄连虽亦入心经，然未免肝脾亦入，未若菖蒲之单入心也。况不杂之以各经之品，孤军深入，又何疑哉！此所以奏功如响也。倘不知用药神机，轻混之以肝脾之药，虽亦奏功，终不能捷如桴鼓。此治热之法也。　　口舌生疮者，乃心经热也，宜用黄连、黄芩之类凉散之自愈。今不用而用黄蘗、僵蚕各一钱，枳壳烧灰、炙甘草、薄荷、山豆根各五分，为细末，冰片三厘研匀，掺上，一日掺三次，第一日即少快，明日痊愈。[38p]

    The effectiveness of this formula lies not in the Huanglian, but in the Changpu. Changpu specifically targets the heart channel, while Huanglian, though it also enters the heart, necessarily involves the liver and spleen as well, which is not as focused as Changpu’s sole targeting of the heart. Moreover, by not mixing in herbs from various channels, but rather advancing with a singular purpose, there can be no doubt about its efficacy! This is why the results are as immediate as the sound of a drum.

    If one does not understand the strategic use of herbs and lightly mixes them with liver and spleen remedies, although there may still be some effect, it will ultimately not be as quick as a drumbeat. This is how one treats heat.

    For those suffering from sores on the tongue and mouth, it indicates heat in the heart channel, and one should use cooling herbs like Huanglian and Huangqin to promote self-healing. Currently, if one utilizes one qian each of Huangbo and Jiangcan, and half a qian each of burnt Zhiqiao, roasted licorice, mint, and Shandougen, ground into a fine powder, mixed with three li of Bingshu, and taken three times a day, improvement will be noticeable on the first day, with complete healing by the next day.[38p]

    　　　　　黑色

    　　阴寒而直中肾经，舌黑眼闭，下身尽黑，上身尽青，大便出，小便遗，此更危急之证，虽有仙方，恐难全活。而予必欲生之，因定一方，虽不敢曰人尽可救，亦庶几于十人中而救一二人乎？方名心救汤。人参五两，附子一个，白朮半斤，肉桂一两，菖蒲五分，良姜三钱，水煎服。此方参、朮多用者，恐少则力量不能胜任，以驾御夫桂、附之热药也。故必多加而后可望其通达上下，以尽祛周身之寒毒。倘得大便止而小便不遗，便有生机。再进一剂，则眼开而舌黑可去，身黑身青俱可尽解也。苟服药后仍前大小便之不禁，不必再服药，听其身死而已矣。大约此方救此病，十人中亦可救三四人。[39p]

    Black

    Cold and directly affects the kidney meridian; the tongue is black, the eyes are closed, the lower body is entirely black, the upper body is entirely blue. With feces expelled and urine retained, this is a very urgent condition. Although there are heavenly remedies, it is feared that complete recovery is difficult. However, I am determined to save lives, thus I have formulated a prescription. While I can't say that everyone can be saved, perhaps one or two out of ten may be rescued. The prescription is called "Heart Rescue Decoction." Ingredients: five taels of ginseng, one piece of aconite, half a jin of atracylodes, one tael of cinnamon, five fen of calamus, three qian of ginger. Boil in water and take it as a decoction. This prescription uses more ginseng and atracylodes; if used too little, the power may not be sufficient to control the heat of cinnamon and aconite. Thus, it must be increased to hope for clarity throughout the body and to completely expel the cold toxins. If bowel movements are stopped and urine retention occurs, there is a chance of life returning. After taking another dose, if the eyes open and the black tongue clears, both the black and blue conditions can be resolved. If after taking the medicine, the problem of incontinence continues, there is no need to take more medicine; one should simply await death. Generally, this prescription can save about three or four out of ten patients suffering from this illness.[39p]

    　　　　　生刺

    　　人有火盛之极，舌如芒刺，唇口开裂，大渴呼饮，虽非伤寒之证所得，而人患此病，即不身热，亦去死不久也。白虎汤亦可救，但过于太凉，恐伤胃气，往往有热退而生变，仍归于亡，故白虎汤不可轻投也。我有一方，名曰清凉散，元参二两，麦冬一两，甘菊花、青蒿各五钱，白芥子、生地、车前子各三钱，水煎服。此方妙在元参为君，以解上焦之焰；麦冬为臣，以解肺中之热；甘菊、青蒿为佐，以消胃中之火；尤妙车前子、白芥、生地为使，或化痰，或凉血，尽从膀胱以下泻其大热之气。是上下之间无非清凉而火热自散，又不损胃，故能扶危而不至生变也。[40p]

    Severe Heat Condition

    When a person has extreme internal heat, the tongue appears like a thorn, the lips and mouth crack, and there is intense thirst with calls for drink. Even if this condition does not present the symptoms of typhoid, the affected person, despite not having a fever, is not far from death. Bai Hu Decoction can also be effective, but it is excessively cooling, which may harm the stomach qi. Often, the heat may diminish but transform into something more serious, leading to death; therefore, Bai Hu Decoction should not be used lightly.

    I have a prescription called Qingliang San: two liang of Yuan Shen, one liang of Mai Dong, five qian each of Gan Ju Hua and Qing Hao, and three qian each of Bai Jie Zi, Sheng Di, and Che Qian Zi, all boiled in water for consumption. This formula is notable because Yuan Shen is the main ingredient, resolving the flames of the upper jiao; Mai Dong serves as the minister, alleviating heat in the lungs; Gan Ju and Qing Hao act as assistants to extinguish fire in the stomach. Particularly effective are Che Qian Zi, Bai Jie, and Sheng Di, which either transform phlegm or cool the blood, directing excessive heat downward from the bladder. Thus, the body maintains a balance of cooling while dissipating heat without harming the stomach, making it able to support those in crisis without risking transformation into a more severe condition.[40p]

    　　　　　燥裂

    　　亡血之后，口舌燥裂不能饮食者，死。盖亡血自然无血以生精，精涸则津亦涸，必然之势也。欲使口舌之干者重润，必须使精血之竭者重生。补精之方，六味丸最妙，然而六味丸单补肾中之精，而不能上补口舌之津也。虽补肾于下，亦能通津于上，然终觉缓不济急。我今定一奇方，上下兼补，名上下相资汤，熟地、麦冬各一两，山茱萸、沙参、当归、牛膝、葳蕤各五钱，人参、元参各三钱，北五味二钱，车前子一钱，水煎服。此方补肾为君，而兼以补肺之药，子母相资，上下兼润，精生而液亦生，血生而津亦生矣，安在危亡之证不可庆再生耶？[41p]

    Dryness and Cracking

    After the loss of blood, if the mouth and tongue are dry and cracked, making it impossible to eat or drink, death will ensue. This is because the loss of blood naturally leads to a lack of blood to produce essence; when essence is depleted, fluids are also depleted, which is an inevitable consequence. To restore moisture to the dry mouth and tongue, it is necessary to rejuvenate the depleted essence and blood. The Six Flavor Pill is the best method to replenish essence; however, it only supplements the essence in the kidneys and cannot nourish the fluids of the mouth and tongue. Although supplementing the kidneys can also facilitate the upper fluids, it still feels inadequate in urgent situations.

    I now propose a remarkable formula that supplements both the upper and lower parts, named the "Mutual Nourishment Decoction". It consists of 1 liang each of prepared Rehmannia and Ophiopogon, and 5 qian each of Cornelian cherry, Adenophora, Angelica, Achyranthes, and Polygala, along with 3 qian each of Ginseng and thyme, 2 qian of Chinese schisandra, and 1 qian of Plantago seeds, decocted in water for administration. This formula primarily supplements the kidneys while also including herbs that nourish the lungs, so that both aspects support each other. It moistens from above and below, leading to the generation of essence and fluids, and hence the generation of blood and fluid. How can one not celebrate the possibility of revival even in critical conditions?[41p]

    　　　　　干肿

    　　燥证舌干肿大，溺血，大便又便血不止，亦是死证。盖感暑热之毒，至秋而燥极，肺金清肃之令不行，大小便热极而齐便血也。论理见血宜治血矣，然而治血，血偏不止，反至燥添而不可救。吾不治血，专治燥，方用兼润丸，熟地、当归、白芍各一两，元参、麦冬、沙参各二两，车前子、生地各五钱，地榆三钱，水煎服。一剂轻，二剂血止，便有生机也。此方纯是补血妙品，惟用地榆以清火，车前子以利水，火清水利，不必治血，血自治也。
    　　　　　吐出

    　　如人舌吐出，不肯收进，乃阳火盛强之故，以冰片少许点之，即收。后用黄连、人参、白芍各三钱，菖蒲、柴胡各一钱，水煎服，二剂可也。[42p]

    Swelling of the Tongue

    Dryness manifests as a dry and swollen tongue, with blood in the urine and continuous blood in the stool, which indicates a fatal condition. This results from the poisonous heat of summer, which becomes extreme in autumn, preventing the lung's metal from purifying and regulating. Consequently, both urine and stool become extremely hot and lead to blood. According to theory, upon seeing blood, one should treat it; however, treating the blood causes it to not cease, adding to the dryness and rendering it hopeless. Therefore, I do not treat the blood directly but focus on alleviating the dryness, using a formula called "Jianrun Pills." The ingredients are one tael each of cooked Rehmannia, Angelica, and white peony, two taels each of Scrophularia, Ophiopogon, and Adenophora, five qian each of Plantago and fresh Rehmannia, and three qian of Chinese rhubarb, all decocted in water. One dose is light, two doses can stop the bleeding, thus bringing hope for recovery. This formula is purely excellent for nourishing the blood, using Chinese rhubarb to clear heat and Plantago to facilitate water flow. With the heat cleared and water facilitated, treating the blood is unnecessary, as it will resolve itself.

    Protruding Tongue

    If a person's tongue is protruding and refuses to retract, it is due to excessive yang fire. Applying a small amount of borneol can help retract it. Later, administer three qian each of Coptis, ginseng, and white peony, and one qian each of sweet flag and bupleurum, decocted in water; two doses should suffice.[42p]

    　　　　　缩入

    　　如人舌缩入喉咙，不能语言，乃寒气结于胸腹之故，急用人参三钱，白朮五钱，肉桂、附子、干姜各一钱治之，则舌自舒矣。
    　　　　　断者可续

    　　凡人有被人咬落舌尖，或连根咬断者，或一日，或二日，或半月，俱可接之。速用狗舌一条，观其人舌之大小切正如人舌光景，将病人舌根伸出，病人坐在椅上，仰面头放在椅背上，以自己手拿住喉咙，则舌自伸出，急将狗舌蘸药末，接在人舌上，一交接永不落矣。末药方开后：龙齿、人参俱透明者，生地各三钱，冰片三分，象皮一钱，土狗三个去头翅，地虱二十个。先将人参各项俱研末，后用地虱、土狗捣烂入前药末内，捣之，佩身上三日，干为末，盛在瓶内。遇有此等病为之医治可也。此药末接骨最奇，服下神效。骨断者服一钱即愈，神方也。[43p]

    Contraction of the Tongue

    When a person's tongue retracts into the throat and they are unable to speak, it is due to cold energy obstructing the chest and abdomen. One should urgently use three qian of ginseng, five qian of white atractylodes, and one qian each of cinnamon, aconite, and dried ginger to treat this, then the tongue will relax.

    Reattachment of a Severed Tongue

    If a person's tongue tip is bitten off or the root is severed, whether it has been one day, two days, or half a month, it can all be reattached. Quickly take a dog’s tongue and ensure its size and cut match the man's tongue. Have the patient sit in a chair, leaning back with their head against the chair, and hold their throat with their hand to extend the tongue. Dip the dog's tongue in medicinal powder and place it on the human tongue; once connected, it will not fall off. The medicinal powder recipe is as follows: three qian each of dragon teeth and ginseng, three fen of borneol, one qian of elephant skin, and three headless and wingless earth dogs, plus twenty earth lice. First, grind all items of ginseng into powder, then mash the earth lice and earth dogs into the preceding powder, mix well, and wear this powder on the body for three days. When dried, store it in a bottle. This medicinal powder is remarkably effective for such conditions. A broken bone will heal with one qian; this is a miraculous remedy.[43p]

    　　　　　绝者可长

    　　闻人说咬落舌头者，以酢漱之，可以重长，此说甚谬。夫肉逢酸则缩，岂有反伸出之理？当用人参一两，煎汤含漱半日，以一两参汤漱完，然后已。再用龙齿末、血竭末各三分，人参未、麦冬末各一钱，冰片二分，土狗一个，地虱十个，各火焙为末，放在土地上一刻，出火气，将此末乘人参漱口完时，即以此末自己用舌蘸之，使令遍，不可将舌即缩入口中，放在外者半刻，至不能忍然后缩入可也。三次，则舌伸长矣。[44p]

    The one who is severed can be long again.

    I have heard people say that one can regrow a lost tongue by rinsing it with vinegar; this claim is highly erroneous. When flesh encounters acidity, it contracts—how could it possibly stretch out again? Instead, one should use one tael of ginseng, decoct it into a broth, and rinse with it for half a day. After completing the rinse with the ginseng broth, take three fen each of dragon's teeth powder and blood-resorption powder, and one qian each of ginseng and wheat beards, along with two fen of borneol, one dog, and ten earth worms. Roast these ingredients to a powder, place them on the ground for a moment to release their heat, and when the ginseng rinse is completed, dip your tongue into this powder, spreading it thoroughly. Do not retract your tongue into your mouth immediately; instead, keep it outside for half a moment. Endure until you can no longer stand it before retracting it back in. Repeat this process three times, and the tongue will be extended.[44p]

    　　　　　伤寒相舌秘法

    　　凡见舌系白胎，邪火未甚也，用小柴胡汤解之。舌系黄色者，心热也，可用黄连、栀子以凉之。凡见黄而带灰色者，系胃热也，可用石膏、知母以凉之。凡见黄而带红者，乃小肠膀胱热也，可用栀子以清之。见舌红而白者，乃肺热也，用黄芩、苏叶以解之。见舌黑而带红者，乃肾虚而挟邪也，用生地、元参，又入柴胡以和解之。见舌红而有黑星者，乃胃热极也，宜用石膏以治之；元参、干葛亦可，终不若石膏之妙。见舌红而有白点者，乃心中有邪也，宜用柴胡、黄连以解之，心肝同治也。见舌红而有大红点者，乃胃热而带湿也，须茵陈五苓散以利之。盖水湿必归膀胱以散邪，非肉桂不能引入膀胱，但止可用一二分，不可多入。见舌白胎而带黑点，亦胃热也，宜用石膏以凉之。[45p]

    Secret Methods for Diagnosing Fever Through the Tongue

    When the tongue has a white coat, it indicates that the evil heat is not severe; use Xiao Chai Hu Decoction to resolve it. If the tongue is yellow, it indicates heart heat; one can use Huang Lian and Zhi Zi to cool it. If the tongue is yellow with a grayish hue, this indicates stomach heat; use Shi Gao and Zhi Mu to cool it. If the tongue is yellow with a reddish tint, this indicates heat in the small intestine and bladder; Zhi Zi can be used to clear it. When the tongue is red with a white coating, it indicates lung heat; Huang Qin and Su Ye can be used to resolve it. If the tongue is black with a reddish tint, it indicates kidney deficiency with evil; use Sheng Di and Yuan Shen, adding Chai Hu to harmonize it. A red tongue with black spots indicates extreme stomach heat; Shi Gao should be used to treat it; Yuan Shen and Gan Ge can also be used, but they are not as effective as Shi Gao. A red tongue with white points signifies the presence of evil in the heart; use Chai Hu and Huang Lian to resolve it, treating both the heart and liver. A red tongue with large red spots indicates stomach heat with dampness; Yin Chen Wu Ling San should be used to promote urination. Water dampness must return to the bladder to disperse the evil, and only cinnamon can draw it into the bladder, but only a small amount should be used, not too much. A tongue that is coated white with black spots also indicates stomach heat; Shi Gao should be used to cool it.[45p]

    见舌黄而有黑者，乃肝经实热也，用柴胡、栀子以解之。见舌白而黄者，邪将入里也，急用柴胡、栀子以解之，不使入里，柴胡乃半表半里不可不用之药也。见舌中白而外黄者，乃邪入大肠也，必须五苓散以分水，水分则泄止矣。见舌中黄而外白者，乃邪在内而非外，邪在上而非下，止可加柴胡、枳壳以和解，不可骤用大黄以轻下也；天水加五苓亦可，终不若柴胡、枳壳直中病原；少加天水则更妥，或不加用天水，加五苓散亦可也。见根黄而光白者，亦胃热而带湿也，亦须用石膏为君，而少加天水之品，如猪苓、泽泻之味也。见舌黄而隔一瓣一瓣者，乃邪湿已入大肠，急用大黄茵陈下之，不必用抵当、十枣汤也。若下之迟，则不得而用之。然须辨水与血之分，下水用十枣，下血用抵当也。见舌有红中如虫蚀者，乃水未升而火来乘也，亦须用黄连、柴胡以和解之。[46p]

    If the tongue is yellow with black spots, this indicates excess heat in the liver channel. Use Chai Hu (Bupleurum) and Zhi Zi (Gardenia) to relieve it. If the tongue is white with yellow, this suggests that the pathogen is about to enter the interior; urgently use Chai Hu and Zhi Zi to prevent it from entering the interior, as Chai Hu is a medicine that works both on the exterior and interior and is essential. If the tongue is white in the middle and yellow on the outside, this indicates that the pathogen has entered the large intestine; one must use Wu Ling San (Five-Ingredient Powder) to disperse water. Once the water is dispelled, the diarrhea will stop. If the tongue is yellow in the middle and white on the outside, this shows the pathogen is internal rather than external, upper rather than lower; one should add Chai Hu and Zhi Ke (Bitter Orange) to harmonize and relieve it, and should not abruptly use Da Huang (Rhubarb) for a harsh purge. Tian Shui (Heavenly Water) added to Wu Ling is also acceptable, but it is always better to use Chai Hu and Zhi Ke to directly address the root of the illness; adding a little Tian Shui is more appropriate, or if Tian Shui is not used, Wu Ling San can also be utilized. If the root of the tongue is yellow and glossy white, this indicates heat in the stomach coupled with dampness; one must use Shi Gao (Gypsum) as the principal ingredient, along with a small amount of Tian Shui products, such as Zhu Ling (Polyporus) or Ze Xie (Alisma). If the tongue has yellow spots separated by white, this indicates that damp pathogens have entered the large intestine, and one should promptly use Da Huang and Yin Chen (Virgate Wormwood) to clear it out without needing to use Di Dang or Shi Zao Tang (Ten Jujube Decoction). If the purging is slow, it cannot be used. One must also distinguish between water and blood; use Shi Zao for water, and Di Dang for blood. If the tongue shows red spots like worm bites, this indicates that water has not risen while fire intrudes; one must also use Huang Lian (Coptis) and Chai Hu to harmonize and relieve it.[46p]

    见舌红而开裂如人字者，乃邪初入心，宜用石膏、黄连以解之。见舌有根黑而尖带红者，乃肾中有邪未散，宜用柴胡、栀子以解之。见舌根黑而舌尖白者，乃胃火乘肾，宜用石膏、知母、元参以解之，不必论其渴与不渴，不必问其下利也。舌根黑而舌尖黄者，亦邪将入肾，须急用大黄下之。然须辨其腹痛与不痛，按之腹痛而手不可近者，急下之，否则只用柴胡栀子以和解之。见舌纯红而独尖黑者，乃肾虚而邪火来乘也，不可用石膏汤。肾既虚而又用石膏，是速之死也。当用元参一两或二两以救之，多有能生者。见舌有中心红晕而四围边旁纯黑者，乃君相二火炎腾，急用大黄加生地两许，下而救之，十人中亦可救五六人。见舌有中央灰黑而四边微红者，乃邪结于大肠也，下之则愈，不应则死。[47p]

    If the tongue is red and裂 like a person’s character, it indicates that evil has just entered the heart; gypsum and yellow orchid should be used to resolve it. If the tongue has a black root and a pointed red tip, it indicates that evil in the kidney has not dissipated; Chai Hu and gardenia should be used to resolve it. If the tongue has a black root and a white tip, it indicates that stomach fire is affecting the kidney; gypsum, anemarrhena, and scrophularia should be used to resolve it, regardless of thirst or diarrhea. If the tongue has a black root and a yellow tip, evil is about to enter the kidney, and it is urgent to use rhubarb as a purgative. However, one must differentiate between painful and painless abdominal symptoms; if there is pain and the abdomen cannot be touched, it should be purged urgently, otherwise, only Chai Hu and gardenia should be used to harmonize and resolve it. If the tongue is uniformly red but the tip is black, it indicates kidney deficiency with evil fire invading; gypsum decoction should not be used. If the kidney is already deficient and gypsum is used, it leads to swift death. Instead, one should use one or two taels of scrophularia to save it, as many can survive. If the tongue shows a red center with pure black around the edges, it indicates the dual fires of the monarch and minister rising; urgent use of rhubarb with two portions of fresh earth should be administered to save it, and out of ten, five or six can be saved. If the tongue has a gray-black center with slightly red edges, this indicates evil has become lodged in the large intestine; purging will lead to recovery, while neglect will lead to death.[47p]

    以肾水枯槁不能润之推送，此时又不可竟用熟地补肾之药，盖邪未散不可补，补则愈加胀急，适所以害之也。必邪下而后以生地滋之则可，然亦不可多用也。见舌有纯灰色中间独两晕黑者，亦邪将入肾也，急用元参两许，少加柴胡治之。见舌有外红而内黑者，此火极似水也，急用柴胡、栀子、大黄、枳实以和利之。若舌又见刺，则火亢热之极矣，尤须多加前药。总之内黑而外白，内黑而外黄，皆前证也，与上同治，十中亦可得半生也。惟舌中淡黑而外或淡红，外或淡白，内或淡黄者，较前稍轻，俱可以前法治之，十人中可得八人生也。见舌有纯红而露黑纹数条者，此水来乘火，乃阴证也，其舌胎必滑，必恶寒、恶水，下咽必吐。倘现纯黑之舌，乃死证也，不须治之。水极似火，火极似水，一带纯黑，俱不可治。伤寒知舌之验法便有把握，庶不至临证差悞耳。[48p]

    If the kidney's essence is dried up and cannot be nourished, one should not use nourishing medicines such as cooked rehmannia at this time. This is because the pathogenic factors have not dispersed, and to replenish would only increase the distension and urgency, thus causing harm. It is essential to first expel the pathogens, after which one may use fresh rehmannia to nourish the kidney, but it should be used sparingly. If the tongue appears a pure gray with two black rings in the center, it indicates that the pathogen is about to invade the kidney. In that case, urgent use of a couple of burdock roots with a bit of bupleurum is required. If the tongue shows a red exterior but a black interior, this signifies extreme heat resembling water; one should urgently use bupleurum, gardenia, rhubarb, and bitter orange to harmonize and facilitate. If the tongue also has spikes, it indicates an extreme level of excessive heat, necessitating an increase in the aforementioned medicines. In general, if the interior is black and the exterior is white or yellow, those are similar signs and should be treated accordingly, allowing for a 50% chance of recovery. If the tongue is a light black with slight red or white on the exterior, or light yellow on the interior, this is a milder condition, and the previous methods can be applied, offering an 80% chance of recovery among ten individuals. If the tongue is purely red with a few black lines, this indicates water attacking fire, which is a yin syndrome; the tongue coating must be slippery, with aversions to cold and water, resulting in nausea and vomiting. Should a pure black tongue appear, that indicates a lethal condition, and no treatment is necessary. Water resembling fire and fire resembling water, both with a pure black hue, should not be treated. Understanding the symptoms as they relate to tongue diagnosis in typhoid allows one to navigate clinical cases more accurately and avoid missteps.[48p]

    　　　　方

    　　升麻煎 【《千金方》，下同】 　治心脏热，舌生疮裂破，引唇揭赤，服之泻热。　　升麻　射干各三两　柏叶切，一升　大青二两　生元参汁三合　苦竹叶切　地黄汁　生芦根　蔷薇根白皮各五两　　右十味(口父)咀，以水四升，煮取一升，去滓；下元参汁，令两沸；次下地黄汁，两沸；次下蜜，煎取一升七合。绵染取汁，安舌上含，细细咽之。　　又方　治舌上疮，不得食，舌本强，颈两边痛，此是心虚热所致。　　柴胡　升麻　芍药　栀子仁　通草各二两　黄芩　大青　杏仁各两半　生姜　石膏各四两　　右十味(口父)咀，以水一斗九升，煮取三升半，分四服，日三夜一，滓可重煎服之。
    　　黑参丸 【丹溪，下同】 　治口舌生疮，久不愈。　　黑参　天门冬　麦门冬去心，各炒一两　　右为末，炼蜜丸，如弹子大，每用一丸，绵裹，噙化咽津。[49p]

    Formula for Shengma Decoction
    Treats heart heat, sores, and cracks on the tongue, leading to swollen and red lips. Take it to clear heat.
    Ingredients: Shengma (3 taels), Shegan (3 taels), cut Baiye (1 sheng), Daqing (2 taels), fresh ginseng juice (3 he), cut Kizhuye, Dihuang juice, fresh Lugeng, and white-pitted rose root (5 taels each).
    Combine these ten ingredients, grind them, and use 4 sheng of water to boil down to 1 sheng, strain out the dregs; add fresh ginseng juice and bring to a boil twice; then add Dihuang juice, boil twice; lastly, add honey, and boil down to 1 sheng 7 he. Soak a cotton ball in the juice, place it on the tongue, and swallow slowly.

    Another Formula
    For treating sores on the tongue with inability to eat, with a strong base tongue and pain on both sides of the neck, caused by heart deficiency heat.
    Ingredients: Chaihu (2 taels), Shengma (2 taels), Shaoyao (2 taels), Zhiziren (2 taels), Tongcao (2 taels), Huangqin (2.5 taels), Daqing (2.5 taels), Xingren (4 taels), fresh ginger (4 taels), and gypsum (4 taels).
    Combine these ten ingredients, grind them, and use 1 dou 9 sheng of water to boil down to 3 sheng 5 he, divide into four doses, take three times in the day and once at night; the dregs can be boiled again.

    Heishen Pills
    Treats sores in the mouth and on the tongue that do not heal for a long time.
    Ingredients: Heishen, Tianmendong, and Maidong (with the core removed, each roasted) (1 tael each).
    Grind these into a powder, mix with honey to form pills the size of a bullet; take one pill at a time, wrap it in cotton, dissolve it in the mouth, and swallow the saliva.[49p]

    Effective Remedies for Pre-existing Conditions
    A small amount of vermilion, realgar, borax, camphor, and musk: grind into a powder. First, wash the affected area with honey water, then apply this mixture for good results.

    Ice Sugary Pill [from Entry]:
    Treats sores on the tongue and mouth blister. Equal parts of yellow bristle grass, mint, and borax; half the amount of camphor. Grind into a powder, form into honey pills the size of a marble, and dissolve in the mouth.

    Combined Gold Powder [from Three Causes]:
    Treats sores on the tongue and mouth. Equal parts of coptis and asarum: grind into powder, dip a cloth in water to cleanse the affected area, then apply the medicine; spitting foaming results in healing.

    Bi Xue [from Effective Result]:
    Treats sores on the tongue, strong tongue, swollen cheeks, and throat obstruction. Equal parts of catkins, indigo, borax, nitre, and licorice: grind into powder, use a finger to apply in the mouth, swallow saliva.

    Aromatic Sand Six Gentlemen Decoction:

    Bixue (from "Heji")
    Used to treat accumulated heat, sores on the mouth and tongue, restlessness, and throat blockage.

    Ingredients: 400 grams each of wine-mixed cooked Rehmannia, which is steamed and dried nine times; 400 grams each of wine-moistened Coriaria, yam, and Poria; 300 grams each of Peony and Alisma.
    Preparation: Grind into fine powder, form into honey pills, and take on an empty stomach.

    Eight-Flavor Pill: Treats ascending deficiency fire, leading to sores in the mouth and tongue.
    Ingredients: Same as Six-Flavor Pill but with an additional 100 grams each of Aconite and Cinnamon.
    Preparation: Grind into fine powder, form into honey pills, and take with saline water on an empty stomach.[57p]

    　　加味归脾汤　治思虑动火，口舌生疮。　　人参　白朮土炒　茯神　枣仁炒　龙眼肉各二钱　木香　甘草炙，各五分　柴胡六分　远志　丹皮　当归酒洗，各一钱黄芪蜜炙，一钱半　山栀八分　姜枣煎服。

    Jiawei Guipi Decoction: Treats excessive thinking that ignites fire, leading to sores on the tongue and inside the mouth. Ingredients: Ginseng, fried Bai Zhu, Fu Shen, fried Zao Ren, Longan flesh, each two qian; Mu Xiang, honey-fried Gan Cao, each five fen; Chai Hu six fen; Yuan Zhi, Dan Pi, and Dang Gui, each one qian; honey-fried Huang Qi, one and a half qian; Shan Zhi eight fen. Decoction with ginger and dates for drinking.

    Yuanshen Shengma Decoction: Treats heat stagnation in the heart and spleen, leading to sores on the tongue, swelling of the tongue, or swelling and pain in the cheeks and neck. Ingredients: Yuanshen, Shengma, Xijiao, Jie geng, Guanzhong, Chi Shao, Huang Qin, and Gan Cao, each in equal parts. Decoction: Four qian per dose, with one and a half cups of water, simmer for seven parts, strain, and can be taken at any time.

    Qing Re Hua Tan Decoction: Treats heat in the upper jiao, excess phlegm causing thirst, and swelling and pain in the mouth and tongue. Ingredients: Bei Mu, Tian Hua Fen, fried Zhi Shi, and Jie geng, each one qian; Huang Qin and Chuan Huang Lian, each one and two-fifths qian; Yuanshen and Chuan Shengma, each seven fen; Gan Cao five fen. Decoction for drinking.

    Ba Zhen Decoction: Treats deficiency of both qi and blood leading to sores on the tongue and inside the mouth. Ingredients: Ginseng, fried Bai Zhu, and Fu Ling, each two qian; honey-fried Gan Cao one qian; Sheng Di, Dang Gui (washed with wine), and fried Shao Yao, each two qian; Chuan Xiong one and a half qian. Decoction for drinking.[58p]

    　　金沸草散　世医用此发散伤寒伤风，及加杏仁五味子治咳嗽，皆效。独未知用之治舌肿牙疼。辛未年，有人患舌肿满塞，粥药不入，其势危甚，煎此一剂，乘热以纸笼气熏之，遂愈。　　前胡　旋覆花各一两　赤芍炒　甘草各一钱　荆芥穗一两半　赤茯苓六钱半　炙半夏五钱　　右水煎服。

    　　右(口父)咀，每服三钱，水一盏，煎至七分，食后温服。
    　　马牙硝丸　治木舌。

    　　牛黄散　治舌肿强。

    Jin Fei Cao San: This is used by physicians to disperse chills and fevers, and when combined with apricot kernels and schisandra, it treats coughs effectively. However, it is unknown how it is used for treating tongue swelling and toothache. In the year of Xinwei, someone suffered from severe swelling of the tongue, with food and medicine unable to enter. The situation was critically dangerous; after boiling this one dose and using hot air to fumigate with paper, they recovered.

    Ingredients:

    • Qian Hu: 1.5 ounces
    • Xuan Fu Hua: 1.5 ounces
    • Chao Chi Shao: 0.5 ounces
    • Gan Cao: 0.1 ounces
    • Jing Jie Sui: 1.5 ounces
    • Chi Fu Ling: 0.65 ounces
    • Zhi Ban Xia: 0.25 ounces

    Boil the above in water and take it.

    Huang Yao Tang: This treats tongue swelling and heavy tongue.

    • Huang Yao & Zhi Gan Cao: 1 ounce each

    Mouthfully chew, take 3 coins worth, boil with 1 cup of water until reduced to 70%, and take warm after meals.

    Ma Ya Xiao Wan: This treats a wooden tongue.

    • Ma Ya Xiao: 7.5 grams
    • Qian Bai Shuang
    • Tai Yin Yuan Jing Shi
    • Han Shui Shi
    • She Xiang, finely ground: 0.5 ounce each
    • Ku Bai Fan: 1.2 grams
    • Zhi Gan Cao: 2.5 grams

    Make into a fine powder, mix well, refine with honey into pills the size of a bullet, and let dissolve in saliva when swallowed.

    Niu Huang San: This treats swelling and stiffness of the tongue.

    • Niu Huang: finely ground
    • Han Fang Ji: 7.5 grams
    • Xi Jiao Pie: 2.5 grams
    • Sheng Di Huang
    • Ling Yang Jiao Pie
    • Ren Shen
    • Gui Xin
    • Zhi Ba Bo Zi: 0.5 ounce each

    Make into a fine powder, mix well, take 3 coins worth, boil with 1 medium cup of water until reduced to 60%. It can be taken anytime warm, with the dregs.[59p]

    　　右研细末，捻糟茄自然汁调。若口噤，挑开灌之妙。

    　　百草霜散　治舌肿起如猪胞，忽然硬肿，逡巡塞闷杀人。　　百草霜不拘多少
    　　右一味，以酢调厚敷舌上下，脱去更傅，须臾即消。若先决去血汁再敷之，尤佳。
    　　乌犀膏　治重舌木舌。

    Flying alum powder treats a wooden tongue. White alum and flying powder, each one part, ground finely together, mixed with natural juice from mashed eggplant. If the mouth is closed, pry it open and administer the mixture.

    Insect powder treats the previous symptoms. Use five pieces of the insect, roasted, with half a tael of salt. Grind them finely, boil with two cups of water until ten boils, strain out the residue, then heat and hold in the mouth to expectorate; the treatment is based on the degree of recovery.

    Herbal frost powder treats a tongue swollen like a pig's bladder, suddenly hard and swollen, causing obstruction and suffocation. The amount of herbal frost is not fixed. Use one ingredient, mix with vinegar, and apply it thickly on the top and bottom of the tongue, replacing it once it is removed; it will dissipate shortly. If you first drain any blood and then apply it, it is even better.

    Black rhinoceros ointment treats heavy tongue and wooden tongue. Two pods of soap tree, crushed, soaked in three sheng of water for a long time, strained to remove the residue, placed in a vessel and boiled down to an ointment. Fire salt, herbal frost powder, ginseng powder, each one qian; good wine one he; white frost plum and borax each in small quantity, ground together and mixed into the ointment. Use a coarse cloth soaked in water to wipe the tongue while cold; then rub with slices of fresh ginger; afterward, use a goose feather to apply a small amount of medicine on the top and bottom of the tongue to expel any stubborn phlegm; chew two inches of licorice, swallow the juice and saliva.[60p]

    Bovine Gall Powder: Treats swollen tongue.
    Ground bovine gall, ginseng, stir-fried rhubarb, ground musk, and roasted licorice, each ½ tael. Skin off 7.5 qian of white poria, ground cinnabar, and sliced and roasted angelica, each 2.5 qian. Mix these into a fine powder. Take 2 qian each time, dissolve in hot broth after meals, and for severe cases, add 1 qian.

    Alum Powder: Treats wind-cold-dampness, with tongue rigid and unable to speak.
    Dried alum and cinnamon heart in equal parts. Grind into powder, and take 1 qian under the tongue each time.

    Sweet Dew Decoction: Treats sores in the mouth and tongue, teeth, and heart heat.
    Equal parts of loquat leaves, dendrobium, scutellaria, raw rehmannia, and roasted licorice after removing the hearts. For these, chop and grind, take 5 qian each time, with 2 sheng of water, boil down to 8 parts, strain, and take warm at any time.

    (Grass-Tongue) Trichosanthes Root Powder: Treats wind-heat dryness in the mouth, with tongue cracking and sores.
    (Grass-Tongue) trichosanthes root, hu huanglian, and scutellaria, each 7.5 qian. Stir-fried silkworms, white lichen skin, and stir-fried rhubarb, each ½ tael. Ground bovine gall and talc, each 2.5 qian. Mix into a fine powder, thoroughly ground, take 2 qian each time, at any time, dissolved in bamboo leaf broth.[61p]

    　　甘露丸　治口舌干燥，解壅毒，退风热。　　寒水石二斤，烧令赤，摊于地上一宿，以出火毒　铅霜细研　龙齿细研　甘草炙赤，各七钱半　马牙硝三两，细研　　右为细末，研匀，以糯米饭和丸，如弹子大，每服半丸，食后用新汲水磨化服。
    　　芦荟散　治口舌生疮。

    Ganlu Pill: Treats dry mouth and tongue, resolves toxic stagnation, and alleviates wind-heat.
    Two pounds of cold water stone, heated until red, spread on the ground overnight to remove fiery toxins.
    Fine ground lead frost, dragon teeth, and licorice (roasted until red), each seven and a half qian.
    Three liang of horse tooth salt, finely ground.
    Combine the components into a fine powder, mix well, and use glutinous rice to form into pills the size of pellets. Take half a pill after meals with freshly drawn water.

    Aloe Powder: Treats oral ulcers.
    Each half liang of aloe, sweet wormwood, toad venom, and goat's foot flower; one and two-tenths qian of ground musk, calcined alum, and ground cow bile; three dried snails, twenty gourd stems, two and a half qian each of fine xixin, clove, and vermilion; seven and a half qian of ground horse tooth salt; one qian of ground bear gall.
    Combine into a fine powder, mix well. First wrap hair around a finger and dip in warm water, using soft fabric to absorb pus. Take a small amount of the powder and sprinkle it on the ulcer. If mild, the toad venom and aloe can be omitted. Adjust based on the severity of the condition.

    Yuan Shen Powder: Treats oral ulcers and painful, decaying gums.
    Equal parts of yuan shen, sheng ma, du huo, huang qin, huang bai, stir-fried da huang, qian hu, rhinoceros horn, mai dong, and gardenia seeds, and roasted licorice.
    Grind into a powder; take five qian with one cup of water, decoct for five minutes, and drink warm at any time.[62p]

    Green clouds disperse; treat sores on the tongue.
    Copper green and lead white frost in equal parts.
    Grind finely and mix a small amount to apply to the tongue.

    Shen Gui Zhi Yin Pill treats atrophy of the legs and undue stretching of the tongue.
    Roast tortoise shell, four taels; stir-fry Anemarrhena with wine; stir-fry Berberis and red plant, each two taels; wash epimedium with wine; one tael each of goji berries and Schisandra; half a tael of dried ginger; grind all into powder, add water to form pills the size of dawn seeds. Take seventy pills, swallowed with warm salt water on an empty stomach.

    Tong Tian Yu Feng Decoction treats the previous symptoms.
    Three qian of Platycodon; one qian each of Ginseng, South Star, and heart-removed Fritillaria. Each five fen of Forsythia, licorice, Saposhnikovia, and ephedra spike; fifteen seeds of (causticum) loquat; one and a half qian of Atractylodes; three slices of fresh ginger; with one and a half bowls of water, decoct to seven parts, remove dregs, add one sip of ephedra and a little ginger juice, take on half an empty stomach, swallow fifty pieces of Qingxin Daotan Pill.

    Qingxin Daotan Pill treats the previous symptoms.
    Half a tael each of South Star and Pinellia processed with ginger; one tael each of Tianhua Fen and white Aconite; seven and a half qian each of stir-fried Coptis and Curcuma; two qian of salt processed black Aconite; half a tael each of stir-fried silkworm (with silk removed), Gastrodia, and Notopterygium. Grind all into powder, mix with ginger juice to form pills the size of dawn seeds. Take fifty pills, swallowed with Tong Tian Yu Feng Decoction.[63p]

    Li Yin Decoction
    Used to treat both Qi and physical illnesses when both are deficient. It addresses cold water invading the heart, and when the yang is unable to contain itself; indicated by a black tongue.
    Ingredients:

    • Angelica (Dang Gui) 2-3 qian or 5-7 qian
    • Dried ginger, stir-fried to yellow, 1-2-3 qian
    • Cooked rhizome (Shu Di) 3-5-7 qian or 1-2 liang
    • Honey-fried licorice (Zhi Gan Cao) 1-2 qian
    • Water, 2 sheng, decoct to 7-8 parts, take while hot. Optionally add cinnamon (Rou Gui) 1-2 qian.

    Great Tonic Decoction
    Used to treat the above conditions.
    Ingredients:

    • Ginseng (Ren Shen) 1-2 qian, a maximum of 1-2 liang
    • Chinese yam (Shan Yao) 2 qian
    • Eucommia (Du Zhong) 2 qian
    • Cooked rhizome (Shu Di) 2-3 qian, a maximum of 2-3 liang
    • Angelica (Dang Gui) 2-3 qian; omit if there is diarrhea
    • Chinese wolfberry (Gou Qi) 2-3 qian
    • Honey-fried licorice (Zhi Gan Cao) 1-2 qian
    • Water, 2 sheng, decoct to 7 parts, take warm before meals.

    Yin Reinforcing and Qi Nourishing Decoction
    Used to treat a tongue with a pale coat, indicating Yin deficiency and excessive internal heat, with exterior pathogenic influences unresolved.
    Ingredients:

    • Ginseng (Ren Shen) 1-2-3 qian
    • Angelica body (Dang Gui Shen)
    • Chinese yam (Shan Yao) roasted in wine, 2-3 qian
    • Cooked rhizome (Shu Di) 3-5 qian or 1-2 liang
    • Licorice (Sheng Ma) 3-5 fen; omit if heat rises to the surface
    • Aged tangerine peel (Chen Pi) 1 qian
    • Honey-fried licorice (Zhi Gan Cao) 1 qian
    • Bupleurum (Chai Hu) 1-2 qian; omit if no exterior pathogen
    • Water, 2 sheng; add fresh ginger 3-5-7 slices, decoct to 8 parts, take warm before meals.[64p]

    古今图书集成医部全录卷一百六十

    舌门

    　　　　单方

    　　舌胎白而滑：生姜蘸蜜擦之，或以生姜蜜水洗之。若舌胎黄赤燥濇者，取新青布裹指蘸冷水频频擦之，轻者易脱，重者难脱，必须大下之，津液还而胎自退矣。【《入门》】
    　　舌上生疮，或白胎干濇如雪，语话不真：薄荷自然汁与白蜜等分，调匀敷之，良。先以生姜厚片蘸蜜水揩洗，后敷药。【《三因》】　　又方：生姜蜜水揩洗，后用朱砂、雄黄、硼砂、脑麝各少许为末敷，亦良。 【《得效》】
    　　补舌断方：治大人小儿偶含刀在口，割断舌头，已垂落而未断。用鸡子白软皮袋了舌头，用破血丹蜜调涂舌根断处，却以蜜调蜡，稀稠得所，敷在鸡子皮上，盖惟软能透药性故也。常勤添敷，三日舌接住，方去鸡子皮，只用蜜蜡勤敷，七日痊安。【《医林》】[65p]

    Tongue Gateway

    Single Prescription

    When the tongue is covered with a white and smooth coating, rub it with fresh ginger dipped in honey, or wash it with ginger honey water. If the tongue coating is yellow, red, dry, or thick, take a new piece of blue cloth, wrap your finger, dip it in cold water, and rub it repeatedly. If it is mild, it can be easily removed; if severe, it is difficult to remove, and you must give a strong purge so that the fluids return and the coating will naturally retreat.

    If there are sores on the tongue, or if the white coating is dry and thick like snow, affecting speech: mix equal parts of mint juice and white honey, blend and apply it. First, wash the tongue with thick slices of fresh ginger dipped in honey water, then apply the medication.

    Another formula: wash with ginger honey water, then use a small amount of cinnabar, arsenic, borax, and musk powder mixed together and apply, which is also effective.

    For treating the severed tongue: if an adult or child accidentally bites their tongue, severing it but leaving part still attached, use the soft skin of a chicken egg to wrap the tongue. Mix Xue Dan (blood-quickening) with honey and apply it to the root of the severed tongue. Then prepare a honey-wax mixture, adjusting the thickness as needed, and apply it on top of the chicken skin, as the softness helps the medicine penetrate. Keep applying it diligently; within three days, the tongue will reattach. After that, remove the chicken skin and continue applying the honey-wax mixture diligently for seven days until fully healed.[65p]
